    <a title="Ceilidh" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3229028-ceilidh"><img alt="Ceilidh" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1422140120p2/3229028.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/150591390?book_show_action=true">Feb 25, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ceilidh" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ceilidh" href="/user/show/3229028-ceilidh">Ceilidh</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer150591390" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12108410592762518049">I love Greek mythology. I love Greek tragedies. I love the gods and goddesses and what they all represent and the timeless stories that accompany them. As with all people who love something, I am weary with re-imaginings and modern day updates of these tales. Some can be brilliant and really update the text to fit with the modern era, others can fail miserably. I was holding out hope for Carter’s debut (with a sequel in the works) since I have always been fascinated by the Hades and Persephone m</span>
  <span id="freeText12108410592762518049" style="display:none">I love Greek mythology. I love Greek tragedies. I love the gods and goddesses and what they all represent and the timeless stories that accompany them. As with all people who love something, I am weary with re-imaginings and modern day updates of these tales. Some can be brilliant and really update the text to fit with the modern era, others can fail miserably. I was holding out hope for Carter’s debut (with a sequel in the works) since I have always been fascinated by the Hades and Persephone myth. There’s also a number of Greek tragedy related YA books coming out soon (including the much talked about “Starcrossed” in which the author received a 7 figure advance for what is billed as Percy Jackson for girls) so my interest was piqued enough to request an ARC on GoodReads.<br /><br />There was a phrase I kept using whilst reading the second half of this book – “What a dick move.” I apologise for the lack of eloquence here but it was the only thing I could think about the more this novel went on. To start off it wasn’t bad. It wasn’t brilliant and was definitely following a set pattern of mediocrity but there were a few moments I enjoyed, specifically Kate’s emotions regarding her dying mother. They were handled well and without overtly saccharine bucket-loads of cheap emotional grabs, and it was interesting to see a paranormal YA character dealing with such a difficult problem. Of course, this was quickly shoved aside for the plot, or what substituted for one.<br />For the first half, “The Goddess Test” wasn’t horrifically bad, it was just mediocre. It seemed to be made from a well worn mould of YA fiction – outcast heroine who immediately garners male attention, jealous female antagonist who quickly becomes friend but fits all the clichés of flighty and annoying, mysterious and tormented supernatural figure to serve as love interest, bad boy moments, technical entrapment, etc. I’d read it all before and it wasn’t anything particularly exciting. Kate and Henry’s relationship was very poorly developed and didn’t make a whole lot of sense, not to mention how decidedly dull Henry was. How can you make Hades dull? By making him a moping misunderstood bad boy, that’s how. The Hades-Persephone myth was twisted into a more teen friendly shape where Henry was made into the victim, which bugged me to no end. Then again, these characters are so un-godly it makes sense to twist the myths to fit them.<br />The characters are the story’s main failing for the bigger part. Kate is fine for most of it until she falls into love-struck too-annoying-to-live territory, typical for paranormal YA heroine these days it seems, and Henry is just dull. None of the immortal characters ever seem like fully fleshed out beings, let alone gods. They never convinced me that they were anything more than childish plot devices. The Greek gods could be childish but they could also be ruthless, passionate, cunning, devastatingly dangerous, charming, every other emotion you could think of. Here, the characters just served to keep the meandering plot from going too off-road.<br /><br />And this was all well and good for the most part. Like I said, it was mediocre but not awful. Then we got into the second half and things changed. What made up the supposed plot and the tests that were so important in deciding whether or not a teenage girl was worthy to become an immortal and co-ruler of the Underworld and the dead become more and more contrived to the point where I was rolling my eyes every other page. Not once was I convinced that Kate was goddess material and the so-called tests just made me think that the Olympians need to hire a new manager or something. but the biggest dick move came in the final few chapters, which I am going to spoil because I was so peeved off by them that I need to share my rage.<br /><br />SPOILERS BELOW.<br /><br />I MEAN IT. DON’T BLAME ME IF YOU’RE SPOILED AND DIDN’T WANT TO BE.<br /><br />...<br /><br />Okay?<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[It was all a test.<br /><br />I have this really big problem with books that reveal the hero/heroine is the pawn in a big game of “Fuck You, It Was All Fake.” I hate when it turns out that the character was lied to by absolutely everyone she cared about just so they could have the right results. No matter how badly contrived they are – like Patch manipulating everyone around Nora to get the right results in “Hush Hush” – or how happy the hero/heroine is with the results, I still think it’s a massive dick move to pull. How can one establish a relationship if there is no trust and never was from the beginning? That’s why I sighed “Oh, come on now!” out loud when it was revealed that everything Kate thought she knew – including HER OWN MOTHER DYING! – was constructed solely for her to take the tests to become Persephone number 2. See, Kate’s mother is one of the goddesses testing her so she was never really dying (okay, her human form was dying but she still lives on in some form.) And Kate is okay with everyone lying to her, or as they put it, hiding the truth from her to keep her safe because those are the rules. It was poorly constructed, it was incredibly contrived and it was a pure and simple dick move. It immediately destroyed any sympathies I had had with the book. I just didn’t care anymore. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /> <br />“The Goddess Test” is a mediocre book, chock full of everything one expects from paranormal YA these days, with serviceable prose and a few moments that keep things going amidst the dull characters and meandering plot. But the big reveal that makes everything okay for everyone except the reader just throws my ability to care out the window and frankly, it pissed me off. Can we stop using characters, especially teenage girls, as pawns in stories? Can we treat them with a little more respect than this? I can’t recommend this book, it just doesn’t seem to care about its readers at all, be they Greek mythology fans or not. This book’s left me with the same feeling I felt the very first time I saw the infinitely superior piece of entertainment, “The Wizard of Oz”, when it’s revealed to all be a dream. That wasn’t fair.<br /><br />1/5.<br /><br />“The Goddess Test” will be released in USA on April 19th 2011. I received my ARC from NetGalley.com. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12108410592762518049" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4075427580563124635">I was extremely disappointed with this book. I read the blurb and thought it'd be great and guess what, it wasn't.<br/><br/>This book like <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6068551.Shiver__The_Wolves_of_Mercy_Falls___1_' title='Shiver (The Wolves of Mercy Falls, #1) by Maggie Stiefvater' rel='nofollow noopener'>Shiver</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6487308.Fallen__Fallen___1_' title='Fallen (Fallen, #1) by Lauren Kate' rel='nofollow noopener'>Fallen</a> were Twilight descendents. The writing style is similar as well as the characters. Katherine, oh I'm sorry, <i>Kate</i>(Warning lights already, remember Bella and her Isabella issue?) states she's not particularly pretty but a whole line of jocks notice her. James and Dylan are immediately mesmerized by her and want to hang around her. <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[But if </span></span>
  <span id="freeText4075427580563124635" style="display:none">I was extremely disappointed with this book. I read the blurb and thought it'd be great and guess what, it wasn't.<br /><br />This book like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6068551.Shiver__The_Wolves_of_Mercy_Falls___1_" title="Shiver (The Wolves of Mercy Falls, #1) by Maggie Stiefvater" rel="nofollow noopener">Shiver</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6487308.Fallen__Fallen___1_" title="Fallen (Fallen, #1) by Lauren Kate" rel="nofollow noopener">Fallen</a> were Twilight descendents. The writing style is similar as well as the characters. Katherine, oh I'm sorry, <i>Kate</i>(Warning lights already, remember Bella and her Isabella issue?) states she's not particularly pretty but a whole line of jocks notice her. James and Dylan are immediately mesmerized by her and want to hang around her. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[But if you wanted to argue, they were part of the council judging her so they had to keep a close eye on her <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br /><br />Henry(Hades) is essentially Edward, he is gorgeous, powerful and hates himself. Need I say more? Ava is Alice who's bubbly and enjoys clothes. Kate, on the other hand, hates pretty clothes but is stuffed in them anyway like a human Barbie doll(another Twilight factor)<br /><br />The other thing that really annoyed me was that the author didn't stay true to Greek mythology at all. I love Greek mythology and how <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/15872.Rick_Riordan" title="Rick Riordan" rel="nofollow noopener">Rick Riordan</a> put a new twist on it in his <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/40736-percy-jackson-and-the-olympians" rel="nofollow noopener">Percy Jackson and the Olympians series</a> but still managed to stay true to Greek mythology. The author didn't do that at all, in fact, she murdered it. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ According to the appendix at the back, Calliope who's in love with Henry is Hera. I'm sorry but what? Hera in love with Hades? It would have made far more sense it Henry was Zeus and let's not forget Hera was the goddess of marriage, she wasn't supposed to go around falling in love with people.<br />Let's not forget James who was going to inherit the Underworld when Henry did. Turns out James is Hermes. Hermes, ruler of the Underworld? Did the author do any research at all? Hermes and the Underworld do not mix. At all. Couldn't she have suggested a more realistic choice like Chiron or something? At least someone who actually has a connection to the Underworld. And what is with the building stuff out of French fries— architecture was <i>Athena's</i> field. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> It all stands to show that the author clearly did no research or simply didn't care.<br /><br />If you're a fan of Greek mythology or original story lines, steer away from this book.</span>

<div id="review_145083135" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/145083135" />
    <a title="~Tina~" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2594672-tina"><img alt="~Tina~" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1411474324p2/2594672.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/145083135?book_show_action=true">Feb 01, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="~Tina~" class="user" itemprop="url" name="~Tina~" href="/user/show/2594672-tina">~Tina~</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=mythology">mythology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=read-2011">read-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=cover-crazz">cover-crazz</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=netgalley-edelweiss">netgalley-edelweiss</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=own-copy">own-copy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer145083135" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9956843178281545613">Kate Winters has always had her mother by her side, but now she's dying and Kate is driving to Eden, her mothers childhood home, for her last request. Kate only wants to take care of her mother and spend as much time with her before she goes, but her mother insists she go to school. So Kate reluctantly goes, but is quite content to stay invisible. She's not here to make friends, she's here to take care of her mother.<br/>Soon she meets Henry. Lonely, haunted, and claims to be the god of the Underworl</span>
  <span id="freeText9956843178281545613" style="display:none">Kate Winters has always had her mother by her side, but now she's dying and Kate is driving to Eden, her mothers childhood home, for her last request. Kate only wants to take care of her mother and spend as much time with her before she goes, but her mother insists she go to school. So Kate reluctantly goes, but is quite content to stay invisible. She's not here to make friends, she's here to take care of her mother.<br />Soon she meets Henry. Lonely, haunted, and claims to be the god of the Underworld, Hades, and while Kate thinks he's crazy, she can't deny that he's brought back a (sorta) friend of hers back from the dead right before her eyes. But at a price.<br />If he could bring Ava back, does that mean he has the power to save her mother? Henry strikes a bargain with Kate, and if she passes the seven tests, she becomes his wife, and a goddess, but if she fails, then she will loss so much more then she ever thought possible.<br /><br />Do you know the story of Persephone?<br />~She was playing in a field when Hades kidnapped her and forced her to stay with him. The land got cold while she was away. She wouldn't eat or drink. Her mother Demeter, pleaded with Zeus on her behave, and eventually Zeus made Hades give her back if indeed she hasn't eaten or drunk anything from the land of dead, but as it turns out, Persephone ate some seeds, so it was agreed that she could spend six months with her mother above ground, but she would also have to spend the other six months with Hades, as his queen.<br />It is the story of how the seasons came to be.<br /><br />Aimee Carter breaks in the world of Greek Mythology and captures the legend of Hades and Persephone, weaving it into brilliance and beauty in her remarkable debut, <b>The Goddess Test</b>.<br /><br />I've always loved, loved, loved, Mythology. I loved that hate and passion and the creation and destruction of it all. It's always been an element I've been fascinated with, so I went into this book with high hopes and was so glad that it did not disappoint.<br />Carter brings something fresh and exciting into this awesome world and I absolutely loved every minute of it.<br /><br />I really enjoyed all the characters, in fact there wasn't one I didn't like. Each and every single one of these characters are beyond thrilling, each has there own unique role and each have a part they play, and I gotta tell you, these characters weren't anything I ever expected once this book was said and done. It's just...WoW!<br />~Kate Winters is an extraordinary character. I so adore her strength and tolerance. I mean, look at all the things she's went through? She couldn't bare to see anyone she loved or cared about or even hated, die. She is the most selfless character that I have ever meet and I loved that through it all, she stayed true to herself.<br />~Henry is simply amazing! Truly loved him to bits. There is a kindness to Henry that was such a wonder to see in the god of Underworld, and quite refreshing I might add.<br />When you think of Hades, you think cruel, dominating and well, evil, but instead we get someone tortured and haunted by past failures with a guilt-ridden heart but there is almost like an underlining of hope that lingers when every he speaks or moves or touches. He's captured in a way that is so breathtaking and heartbreaking that it's completely mesmerizing. Such a fascinating creature.<br /><br />While the storyline wraps around the myth of Persephone, it's shaped in a different way. This is the stuff I love about books. Authors get to break away from traditional folklore and create something unique and bright and amazing. But I can also understand that some readers may not like the idea of there favorite mythology characters being taken out of there original design and conveying them in a different light, but for me, I had a blast with this concept!! I loved the entire set-up to this world and that ending had me completely floored! It shocked and awed me at the same time. Freaking Kudos!<br /><br />Simply put. I loved this book! It has everything I look for in an escape. Unique, romantic, mysterious, compelling and ingenious. I was captivated from the very first page, till the very last and all I want is <i>more</i>.<br />An instant favorite! I can't wait to see what Carter has planned next in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10114414.Goddess_Interrupted__Goddess_Test___2_" title="Goddess Interrupted (Goddess Test, #2) by Aimee Carter" rel="nofollow noopener">Goddess Interrupted</a>. Is it 2012 yet?!?!<br /><br />A Remarkable debut!!<br /><br />(Big thanks to NetGalley and Harlequin Teen for giving me an opportunity to view an early copy of this amazing read)<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9956843178281545613" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8265057040079180173">I'm rating this book 3.25 stars. This book was good. Originally I thought the tests would be more dramatic and not as underwhelming as they were. That was a bummer. But the way the author did do the tests which was do them in plain sight without the heroine knowing was interesting. Overall I liked this and it was a quick read.   <span id="freeText8265057040079180173" style="display:none">I'm rating this book 3.25 stars. This book was good. Originally I thought the tests would be more dramatic and not as underwhelming as they were. That was a bummer. But the way the author did do the tests which was do them in plain sight without the heroine knowing was interesting. Overall I liked this and it was a quick read. One thing I didn't like was that Kate was so selfless. Yes. Yes. I know that's what most heroines are made of. But what really bothered me was that to save Ava's life after Ava abandoned her and the only way to get out was by passing her worst fear (water/swimming)Ava fell in and even though I would have tried to save her like the heroine. I wouldn't have offered to spent six months out of the year for the rest of my life to bring her back from the dead. So I do wish that Kate did have some self preservation. I liked Henry. What I really liked about this book was how the author put a twist on the classic story of Hades and Persephony. The Greek mythology was mixed really well in this book. The love story I was kind of like how? How did Kate fall in love with Henry. I felt no romantic or physical connection between both characters. And I would have liked it to be more falling slowly and passionately in love. But it was good not great but good.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6828898854357163428">Aimee Carter is a debut author (and only 24 years old!) and her Goddess Test series is definitely one to watch for (planning on being a three book series...so far; GODDESS INTERRUPTED will follow in February 2012). <br/><br/>To start with, I felt abashed that this book made me cry so easily! The book opens with protagonist Kate and a rundown of her role as caregiver for her dying mom. Carter's description of this heart-wrenching process is mature and well-written. <br/><br/>This book also pays homage to one of my f</span>
  <span id="freeText6828898854357163428" style="display:none">Aimee Carter is a debut author (and only 24 years old!) and her Goddess Test series is definitely one to watch for (planning on being a three book series...so far; GODDESS INTERRUPTED will follow in February 2012). <br /><br />To start with, I felt abashed that this book made me cry so easily! The book opens with protagonist Kate and a rundown of her role as caregiver for her dying mom. Carter's description of this heart-wrenching process is mature and well-written. <br /><br />This book also pays homage to one of my favorite myths, the myth of Persephone. I've been in love with pomegranates ever since first reading this myth, but Kate feels different about the seeds. She also feels differently about the prospect of spending eternity with Hades (who is a hottie!), but I won’t give away whether she disdains or enjoys his company. <br /><br />But I will say, there is one big twist at the end and of course, the ending of the novel has me reeling to read the next book in the series, GODDESS INTERRUPTED. <br /></span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jennifer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jennifer" href="/user/show/2473504-jennifer">Jennifer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/11140407-the-goddess-test">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2473504-jennifer?shelf=authors-first-novel-debut">authors-first-novel-debut</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2473504-jennifer?shelf=mythology">mythology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2473504-jennifer?shelf=read-2015">read-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2473504-jennifer?shelf=young-adult-genre">young-adult-genre</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2473504-jennifer?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer595607186" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13611669835874043262"><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9681214.The_Goddess_Test__Goddess_Test___1_' title='The Goddess Test (Goddess Test, #1) by Aimee Carter' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Goddess Test</a> is the first installment in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/767317.Aimee_Carter' title='Aimee Carter' rel='nofollow noopener'>Aimee Carter</a>'s young adult, fantasy trilogy titled <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17622949.The_Goddess_Test_Boxed_Set_The_Goddess_Test__Goddess_Interrupted__The_Goddess_Inheritance_The_Goddess_Legacy' title='The Goddess Test Boxed Set The Goddess Test, Goddess Interrupted, The Goddess Inheritance,The Goddess Legacy by Aimee Carter' rel='nofollow noopener'>Goddess Test</a>. I've had this title on my TBR list for quite a while but never picked it up until it coincidentally became BOTM on one of the goodreads groups I participate in. Don't you love it when you get a little nudge to knock a book off that long list!<br/><br/>Overall, I liked <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9681214.The_Goddess_Test__Goddess_Test___1_' title='The Goddess Test (Goddess Test, #1) by Aimee Carter' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Goddess Test</a>. I enjoy mythology, and despite the title (duh!), I didn't expect the book to incorporate so much of the subject s</span>
  <span id="freeText13611669835874043262" style="display:none"><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9681214.The_Goddess_Test__Goddess_Test___1_" title="The Goddess Test (Goddess Test, #1) by Aimee Carter" rel="nofollow noopener">The Goddess Test</a> is the first installment in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/767317.Aimee_Carter" title="Aimee Carter" rel="nofollow noopener">Aimee Carter</a>'s young adult, fantasy trilogy titled <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17622949.The_Goddess_Test_Boxed_Set_The_Goddess_Test__Goddess_Interrupted__The_Goddess_Inheritance_The_Goddess_Legacy" title="The Goddess Test Boxed Set The Goddess Test, Goddess Interrupted, The Goddess Inheritance,The Goddess Legacy by Aimee Carter" rel="nofollow noopener">Goddess Test</a>. I've had this title on my TBR list for quite a while but never picked it up until it coincidentally became BOTM on one of the goodreads groups I participate in. Don't you love it when you get a little nudge to knock a book off that long list!<br><br>Overall, I liked <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9681214.The_Goddess_Test__Goddess_Test___1_" title="The Goddess Test (Goddess Test, #1) by Aimee Carter" rel="nofollow noopener">The Goddess Test</a>. I enjoy mythology, and despite the title (duh!), I didn't expect the book to incorporate so much of the subject so that in itself was a plus. The cover art is stunning; the story offers fantasy, mystery/suspense, humor, and some young-adult romance. It kept my interest and I felt invested enough in the characters, but the experience was missing the "wow" factor that would warrant a 4 or 5 star rating from me personally. I went with 3 stars, which based on goodreads is not bad- I liked it afterall. I am interested enough to continue the series, but I don't find myself overly eager to continue the trilogy anytime soon. <br><br><b>My favorite quote:</b><br><i>“Sometimes we misjudge what is possible and what is not.”</i><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1420264039i/13199143._SX540_.jpg" width="365" height="100" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="13611669835874043262" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_144842963" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/144842963" />
    <a title="Nic" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2813423-nic"><img alt="Nic" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/144842963?book_show_action=true">Jan 30, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nic" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nic" href="/user/show/2813423-nic">Nic</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2813423-nic?shelf=read-in-2011">read-in-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2813423-nic?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2813423-nic?shelf=paranormal-romance">paranormal-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer144842963" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8406521411930609132">The Goddess Test is an awesome debut. It was a hypnotic yet comfortable read where the pages just flew by.<br/><br/>It is such an eloquently written story that I am surprised that this is Aimee Carter's debut novel. It is just a seamless read and a really remarkable debut. And the premises was incredible. I loved the way the mythology was weaved into the plot. It was creative, unique and easy to follow. And for a book that is part of a series is has a completely satisfying ending. YAY!<br/><br/>Kate, the female pro</span>
  <span id="freeText8406521411930609132" style="display:none">The Goddess Test is an awesome debut. It was a hypnotic yet comfortable read where the pages just flew by.<br /><br />It is such an eloquently written story that I am surprised that this is Aimee Carter's debut novel. It is just a seamless read and a really remarkable debut. And the premises was incredible. I loved the way the mythology was weaved into the plot. It was creative, unique and easy to follow. And for a book that is part of a series is has a completely satisfying ending. YAY!<br /><br />Kate, the female protagonist is a likeable and endearing character. She is a compassionate and caring person who will sacrifice anything for those she cares about. And there is a wide variety of secondary characters that are well rounded and entertaining. Okay there were also a couple I found annoying like Ava but overall it was a good bunch of a characters. I especially like James (not a love interest, just a friend....well at least at this stage). He is a little bit different and a mysterious character that I hope we get to see more of in the next installment.<br /><br />The romance was sweet and tender but it lacked a little spark as did Henry. He was a nice guy who I liked but he lacked that something special to make him standout at this stage from all those literary leading men. I really hope that in second book he opens up more as a character and then I am sure I will be swooning. <br /><br />Overall, The Goddess Test has a very familiar paranormal romance feel to it but yet it is different enough to be memorable and a highly enjoyable read. I am certainly eagerly anticipating the next instalment in the series.<br /><br /><i>Thanks to Harlequin Teen for providing me with a copy</i></span>

          </span>

        <a title="Amber" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amber" href="/user/show/3603005-amber">Amber</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3603005-amber?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3603005-amber?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3603005-amber?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer151159430" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12242712578325664220"> What an incredible debut from author Aimee Carter!! The Goddess Test was absolutely amazing!!! I’ve always had a love for Greek Mythology and Aimee has just set the precedence for Greek Mythology lovers.<br/><br/>The story is about a girl named Kate and her mother who is deathly ill. Kate’s mother wants to go back to her hometown where she was born and raised to die. Kate has taken care of her mother for the past four years and that’s all she knows. She doesn’t have a life outside of home and school. Kat</span>
  <span id="freeText12242712578325664220" style="display:none"> What an incredible debut from author Aimee Carter!! The Goddess Test was absolutely amazing!!! I’ve always had a love for Greek Mythology and Aimee has just set the precedence for Greek Mythology lovers.<br /><br />The story is about a girl named Kate and her mother who is deathly ill. Kate’s mother wants to go back to her hometown where she was born and raised to die. Kate has taken care of her mother for the past four years and that’s all she knows. She doesn’t have a life outside of home and school. Kate loves her mother more than anything and will do anything to make her happy in her final days. The story really unfolds when Kate begins school in Eden. When Kate ends up falling victim to a vicious prank she meets Henry, a beautiful, dark and mysterious guy who makes a deal with Kate and now Kate has a bargain to uphold and many choices to make. She faces many hardships but also discovers comforts in other places and people, especially Henry. She is falling for him and is finding she relates to him more than she ever thought. They both have hardships they have been dealt but together they can face them hand in hand.<br /><br />The characters in this story are well defined and well written. Our protagonist, Kate, was an all around amazing character. There wasn’t anything annoying about her and the emotions and the heart she showed was absolutely captivating! This had me on the edge of my seat with a Kleenex box in hand. This book truly pulls you to the core. Henry was yet again, another amazing character. You really learn and understand him better and become so wrapped up in everything he has gone through. I really loved the secondary characters as well. They brought so much to the story. They played such an important part in making it as wonderful as it could be.<br /><br />This is a beautifully written book with such fresh and vivid details you can actually picture the settings and the see the story unfold in your own eyes. I was so captivated by this book. I will definitely be buying this as soon as it comes out. I’m looking forward to the next book Goddess Interrupted. This is a Must read!!! <br /><br />Thank You to NetGalley and Harlequin Teen!!<br /></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/136163511?book_show_action=true">Dec 22, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristi" href="/user/show/1310688-kristi">Kristi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1310688-kristi?shelf=signed-books">signed-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1310688-kristi?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer136163511" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15416204203989550478">I love Greek mythology! I'm a fan of any sort of mythology and folklore, but Greek mythology is one of my favorites! I especially love when an author recreates a myth, spinning an old favorite into something new. There are so many great novels featuring Greek mythology and The Goddess Test has quickly become one of my favorites!<br/><br/>My favorite book despite their subject matter are ones that have great characters, a captivating story like and are well written. The Goddess Test possesses all of those </span>
  <span id="freeText15416204203989550478" style="display:none">I love Greek mythology! I'm a fan of any sort of mythology and folklore, but Greek mythology is one of my favorites! I especially love when an author recreates a myth, spinning an old favorite into something new. There are so many great novels featuring Greek mythology and The Goddess Test has quickly become one of my favorites!<br /><br />My favorite book despite their subject matter are ones that have great characters, a captivating story like and are well written. The Goddess Test possesses all of those qualities and then some!<br /><br />I loved Kate and her dedication to her mother, I loved that she wasn't afraid to speak her mind and that she stood up for the things that she loved and the people that she loved. She was certainly worthy of divine things!<br /><br />And I really liked the romance in this novel, it wasn't a cheesy rush... it was a well paced and realistic. (As it could be!) And although I may have a figured a few things out early, I was still thoroughly engrossed in the story the entire time.... and seeing how it all came together at the end... it was rather brilliant!<br /><br />The Goddess Test was an entertaining and memorable addition the YA books featuring Greek mythology. I can't wait to read the rest of this series! It'll be epic, I'm sure!</span>

<div id="review_217897952" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/217897952" />
    <a title="Sita" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5831199-sita"><img alt="Sita" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1506310723p2/5831199.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/217897952?book_show_action=true">Oct 02, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sita" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sita" href="/user/show/5831199-sita">Sita</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781921794858" href="/book/show/11938582-the-goddess-test">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5831199-sita?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5831199-sita?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5831199-sita?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5831199-sita?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5831199-sita?shelf=teen-romance">teen-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer217897952" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11754002206971942444">I’ve actually been meaning to review this for a while. But I guess I just didn’t know hoe. So, after much care and consideration I have put together this review.<br/><br/><b>I picked this book up because…. </b>I have no idea why I picked this book up. I mean it has gotten some really, really bad reviews. But I guess my subconscious mind wanted me to read it. So I bought it along with Glow and The Girl in the Steel Corset. Out of the three this was the first that I read, I picked it up first and I read it first. </span>
  <span id="freeText11754002206971942444" style="display:none">I’ve actually been meaning to review this for a while. But I guess I just didn’t know hoe. So, after much care and consideration I have put together this review.<br /><br /><b>I picked this book up because…. </b>I have no idea why I picked this book up. I mean it has gotten some really, really bad reviews. But I guess my subconscious mind wanted me to read it. So I bought it along with Glow and The Girl in the Steel Corset. Out of the three this was the first that I read, I picked it up first and I read it first. I started reading it on the bus ride home and I could not put it down. Surprisingly it was really good. Thank you subconscious mind.<br /><br />I’m not going to bore you with the details of the book. <b>So the book in a sentence:</b> Boy (Henry, but actually Hades) saves girl’s (Kate) frenemy (Ava, one of the main characters becomes Kate’s BFF, even though she WAS a bitch) in return for Kate coming back to his lair and becoming his queen, she grudgingly agrees and he says to become a goddess she must pass a bunch of tests (unknown to her), her and Henry fall in love (as would be expected), Kate also has a bunch of threats on her life (by a jealous goddess, she’s in love with Henry). That’s basically the book in a nutshell.<br /><br /><b>The plot was good,</b> if you forget everything you have ever heard or read about Greek Mythology you’ll probably enjoy this more, but even if you cant forget it’s still a good idea and it’s a good plot. I love how it all comes together at the end. I love the moment all the gods and goddesses reveal themselves. I also love when Kate finds out Henry is a virgin and she deflowered him (yep you heard me the almighty god of the underworld was a virgin).<br /><br /><b>I liked the writing,</b> it was likeable. I have never been a good judge at writing, it’s either it kept me interested or it didn’t and this one kept me interested. So if I would have to rate it, I would give the writing 7/10. It kept me interested and I haven’t liked many paranormal romances lately.<br /><br /><b>The characters,</b> I have no clue what to say here. I liked the characters they were all likeably enough; I liked the fact that the God’s were hidden amongst the normal characters. I liked how some of the characters had back-stories. I liked the main character although at times I found her a little unbelievable; she just seemed really two-dimensional at times.<br /><br /><b>Overall,</b> it was an enjoyable read and I finished it in a day and a half. I liked it. I recommend this book to YA paranormal romance likers, you may not love it, but I recommend giving it a go and I don’t recommend it to people that are really invested and love Greek Mythology, you’ll probably just pick the book apart. When on the whole it’s a good book.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11754002206971942444" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1218060185" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1218060185" />
    <a title="Anna (Enchanted by YA)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30983445-anna-enchanted-by-ya"><img alt="Anna (Enchanted by YA)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1426518362p2/30983445.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1218060185?book_show_action=true">Mar 04, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anna (Enchanted by YA)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anna (Enchanted by YA)" href="/user/show/30983445-anna-enchanted-by-ya">Anna (Enchanted by YA)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30983445-anna-enchanted-by-ya?shelf=fell-for-the-hype">fell-for-the-hype</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30983445-anna-enchanted-by-ya?shelf=insta-love-alert">insta-love-alert</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30983445-anna-enchanted-by-ya?shelf=major-disappointment">major-disappointment</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30983445-anna-enchanted-by-ya?shelf=saw-it-all-coming">saw-it-all-coming</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30983445-anna-enchanted-by-ya?shelf=almost-dnf">almost-dnf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30983445-anna-enchanted-by-ya?shelf=cardboard-characters">cardboard-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30983445-anna-enchanted-by-ya?shelf=meh">meh</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30983445-anna-enchanted-by-ya?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1218060185" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6853443722886525546">As an audiobook, the story was told beautifully – the problem is: the story was awful.<br/><br/>From the synopsis I was intrigued by a plot which looked so promising, and it could have been with the intricate references to Greek mythology but the characters ruined it. I couldn’t stand a single one, and even after discovering their true identities (something I predicted from the beginning) they continued to annoy the hell out of me.<br/><br/>Kate was by far the worst. It largely fell down to the fact that she blamed</span>
  <span id="freeText6853443722886525546" style="display:none">As an audiobook, the story was told beautifully – the problem is: the story was awful.<br><br>From the synopsis I was intrigued by a plot which looked so promising, and it could have been with the intricate references to Greek mythology but the characters ruined it. I couldn’t stand a single one, and even after discovering their true identities (something I predicted from the beginning) they continued to annoy the hell out of me.<br><br>Kate was by far the worst. It largely fell down to the fact that she blamed everything on herself. Someone <i>tries</i> to kill her and she feels guilty for the person’s twisted reasoning <i>which wasn’t under her control</i>. Someone basically imprisons her and she blames herself for when things go wrong and they get their just deserts.<br><br>Not only this but she is the most selfless protagonist I have ever read about – and it felt like a bad thing. She never spared a thought about herself, doing everything within her power to aid others when she shouldn’t have had to and they didn’t deserve it anyways! It was unbelievable and frankly unhealthy at times.<br><br>Henry wasn’t much better and they were constantly trying to outdo each other with the “I’m not worth you” nonsense. Arghh I wanted to shake some sense into them! Or at the very least slap them upside the head until they started thinking like normal people. Eventually it turned from me virtually tearing my hair out, to laughing aloud at the idiocy. Needless to say I got some weird looks as I walked along the street muttering to myself.<br><br>It was one of those things where if I didn’t laugh I’d cry; something I didn’t even know was possible in a book, let alone a bad one! I wanted to give The Goddess Test 2 stars for bringing some out sort of emotion, but I can’t. I just can’t, because I can’t recommend this.<br><br>Unless of course you like uninteresting Greek Gods who abide by morals. You heard me – morals. I mean come on, seriously? What myths has Aimee Carter been reading? They murder and sin and marry their family: they don’t “test” mortals by examining their character to see if they are worthy of immortality.<br><br>Unless of course you like bland characters that you want to stab.<br><br>Unless you want predictable “plot twists” STAY AWAY FROM THIS BOOK! You see it in a bookshop and you hide it behind something else before running away; save yourself the time and mental wellbeing. It’s safe to say I won’t be touching the sequel with a ten foot pole.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1428351180ra/14409739.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Posted on: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://enchantedbyya.blogspot.co.uk/">http://enchantedbyya.blogspot.co.uk/</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="6853443722886525546" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_268100751" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/268100751" />
    <a title="Nicola " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2461560-nicola"><img alt="Nicola " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1385858279p2/2461560.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/268100751?book_show_action=true">Jan 26, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nicola " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nicola " href="/user/show/2461560-nicola">Nicola </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781459201699" href="/book/show/11152523-the-goddess-test">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2461560-nicola?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2461560-nicola?shelf=still-reading-series">still-reading-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2461560-nicola?shelf=cover-appeal">cover-appeal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2461560-nicola?shelf=gods-and-goddesses">gods-and-goddesses</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2461560-nicola?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2461560-nicola?shelf=needs-review">needs-review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2461560-nicola?shelf=greek-myths">greek-myths</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer268100751" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1091703928810765957">I really did not know what to expect from this book. I was drawn in by the lovely cover and the description definitely intrigued me. The reviews I'd read hadn't made it look too promising though so I definitely went into it with a cautious mind and didn't expect too much from it. I was seriously delighted to find how much I loved it! I actually adored it from the start and knew it was my kind of thing after the first few chapters.<br/><br/>I am not that into Greek mythology, in general. I know bits and fi</span>
  <span id="freeText1091703928810765957" style="display:none">I really did not know what to expect from this book. I was drawn in by the lovely cover and the description definitely intrigued me. The reviews I'd read hadn't made it look too promising though so I definitely went into it with a cautious mind and didn't expect too much from it. I was seriously delighted to find how much I loved it! I actually adored it from the start and knew it was my kind of thing after the first few chapters.<br /><br />I am not that into Greek mythology, in general. I know bits and find it interesting but I am in no way well educated on it. The only other Greek myth books I've read were not ones I really enjoyed. This was so different though! I was just sucked right into Kate's world. Her mom is dying and her mother's last wish is to move to Eden, her hometown. So they pack up and head to this small town.<br /><br />Kate's just trying to enjoy the little time she has left with her mom and has no time for friends or a social life. She has pushed the rest of the world out so that she can care for her mother. I'll admit that lately I've been getting a bit tired of YA book parents being dead or sick or absent but thankfully this situation turned out to be different than usual and I actually didn't see the twist coming at all!<br /><br />I loved reading about Kate's time in Eden Manor. The concept of the Seven Tests was something that fascinated me as I always like plots like that. All the characters were so awesome though I'll admit Henry did irritate me at times! I get why he was acting like he was but I do think he's had long enough to come to terms with it, really! Kate went back and forth between being dependant and needy and definitely had a desire to play heroine to everyone around her. Which is understandable given that she had so little control over the rest of her life.<br /><br />I was gripped by this whole book and I'm so glad to have found a series that I think I'll actually be able to follow through with for once! I am so excited about the second book and have really high hopes for it.<br /><br /><i>This review first appeared <a href="http://apocketfullofbooks.blogspot.com/2012/02/review-goddess-test-by-aimee-carter.html" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a> on my blog.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="1091703928810765957" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer282538787" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2687974774226350330"><i>
  <b>Original review from <a href='http://littlebookowl.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>Little Book Owl</a></b>
</i><br/><br/>Full video review found here: <a href='http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=D_gNd7qs0y4' rel='nofollow noopener'>Youtube</a><br/><br/><u>The Goddess Test</u> is a unique take on the Persephone and Hades myth. The plot was very intriguing, keeping you in the dark about several mysteries throughout the entire story.<br/><br/>The writing style was quite nice, simple. However there are a couple of questions that still have me a little confused.<br/><br/>I loved Kate. She was a very strong main character with a moral and compassionate attitude. She was selfless, putting her life and</span>
  <span id="freeText2687974774226350330" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>Original review from <a href="http://littlebookowl.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Little Book Owl</a></b>
</i><br /><br />Full video review found here: <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=D_gNd7qs0y4" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a><br /><br /><u>The Goddess Test</u> is a unique take on the Persephone and Hades myth. The plot was very intriguing, keeping you in the dark about several mysteries throughout the entire story.<br /><br />The writing style was quite nice, simple. However there are a couple of questions that still have me a little confused.<br /><br />I loved Kate. She was a very strong main character with a moral and compassionate attitude. She was selfless, putting her life and future on the line for others.<br /><br />Not so sure what to make of Henry. He was very disconnected and distant from Kate, even in the intimate moments. This left the romance feeling a little lacking in depth and character.<br /><br />The side characters were great. I loved James, he was very funny and cute. Would have liked to have seen a little more of him, but his disappearance was understandable due to later twists.<br /><br />Overall, I thoroughly enjoyed this story. I love the Greek mythology, and would highly recommend this book to everyone.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2687974774226350330" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_661602206" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/661602206" />
    <a title="Colette" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1481661-colette"><img alt="Colette" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1427844394p2/1481661.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/661602206?book_show_action=true">Jul 07, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Colette" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Colette" href="/user/show/1481661-colette">Colette</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer661602206" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10843125629153307376">The Goddess Test is a romantic fantasy book that has a good balance between the two, also adding in a healthy dose of mystery and action. Anyone who loves Greek mythology will likely enjoy The Goddess Test. Carter was successful at having the traditional Greek myths mixed with her own fictional touches, though sometimes I felt that the two could have been blended together a bit better. Overall 4/5 stars, and I am looking forward to reading the sequel.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('dhLUvWVCOWhEvJU1nJWvMzY8E4CLeBKO6VZ77WesrfBMNL1v3hzwAOOXIVRrYKXs4GP0SEX1nOmyKD1cqu9fag==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('grQ/jvwUhh3fvDIOUSy/H4CtcVX+CpxnNnFiDVUkf/e4klZcR0pPdXiXhm+m2bXAVvKWnTCHEgBtDyS8mGeNbQ==')})
  }
